Ethyl Acetate Extraction. Place an appropriate aliquot

funnel 1n a beaker of hot water untll the solidlfled portion
dissolves.

After the layers have separated, drain off the aqueous

should not be dralned off. Add 10 ml. of slumlnum nltrate wash

solution to the funnel and agaln shake the mixture for 45 to 60

effect of about 0.005 absorbance (optical density) has some-

Read the absorbance of the sample sclution on the Beckman

DU spectrophotometer at 400 mp against a reference solution

PROCEDURE 7: Uranium-237.
Source: 3B. Warren, LA-1721 (Rev) (1956).

1. Introduction

In the carrler-free method for the determination of y237,
the principal decontamination step (which 1s preceded by a
La(OH) 4 scavenge and partial removal of plutonium as the cup-
ferron complex) 1s the extraction of uranium into 30% TBP
(tertiary butyl phosphate) in benzene. Additional decontam-
ination 1s effected by adsorption of uranium, first on an anion
and then on a catlon exchange resin. The uranlum 1s finally
electroplated on platinum. The chemical yleld is 40 to 60%
and 18 determined through the use of y233 tracer. The g237
1s B-counted 1n a proportional counter with a 2.61-mg/cn Al
absorber, and from the number of counts the number of atoms
of the 1lsotope is calculated. Four samples can be run in

about 6 hours.

three additional times with chloroform. To the aqueous layer

at a vigorous rate.

PROCEDURE 8: Radloassay of Uranium and Plutonium in Vegeta=
tion, Soll and Water.

Source: E. L. Gelger, Health Physics 1, 405 (1959).
Abstract

A method ls discussed for the separation of uranium
and plutonium from vegetatlon, soll and water. The method
is based on the extraction of uranium and plutonium from 4
to 6 N nitric acid into 50% tri-n-butyl phosphate in n-tetra-
decane diluent. Uranlum and plutonlum are recovered together
with sufficient reduction ln total sollds to allow a-counting
and pulse helght analysis. Data from several hundred "splked"
samples to which uranlum and plutonium were added lndicate a
nearly equal recovery of uranlum and plutonium. Average re-
coveries are 76 + 14 per cent for vegetation, 76 = 16 per
cent for soll, and 82 = 15 per cent for water. The procedure

1s designed for samples that may be collected and analyzed

287
PROCEDURE 8 (Continued)

for radloactivity as a part of a health physles reglonal

monitoring program.

Procedures
Preparation of samples

Vegetation. Cut oven-dried vegetation into small pieces
and welgh 10.0 .g into a 150 ml beaker. Heat the sample at
600°C, starting with a cold muffle furnace. When only white
ash remalns, remove the beaker from the muffle furnace and
allow to cool. Carefully add 2 ml of water, then add 10 ml
of 8 XN HNO5=0.5 M A1(NOg)4 solution. Cover the beaker with
a watch glass and boll the solutlon for 5 mln. Allow to cool,
add 1 ml of 2 M KNO, solution and transfer the sample to a
100 ml centrifuge tube. Use 4 N HNOg to complete the transfer.
Centrifuge and decant the supernate into a 125 ml cylindrical
separatory funnel graduated at 30 ml. Wash the residue with
4 N HNO, centrifuge, and decant the wash solution to the
separatory funnel. The acid normality of the combined solu-
tions at this point 1s 4-6 N and the total volume should not
exceed 29 ml. Proceed to the extractlon procedure.

Soll. Grind 5 g of oven-dried soll with a mortar and
peatle untll the entlre sample can pass through a 200-mesh
sleve. Weigh 1.0 g of the 200-mesh soll into a 50 ml platinum
cruclble and heat the sample at 600°C for 4 hr. Remove the
sample from the muffle furnace and allow to cool. Add 3 ml of
70% HNO and 10 ml of 48% HF then stir the sample for 2-3
mln with a platinum rod. Heat the sample in a 200°C sand
bath until all tracee of moisture are removed. Repeat thls
HNO, -HF treatment being careful that the sample 1s completely
dry before proceeding to the next step. Allow the sample to
cool and then add 15 ml of 6 N HNO3-0.25 M A1(NO5),4 solution.

Cover with a watch glass and heat ln the sand bath for 5 min.

288
PROCEDURE 8 (Continued)

Allow to cool and decant the solution through a filter, such
as Whatman no. 40, into a 125 ml oylindrical separatory funnel
graduated at 30 ml. Leave as much of the resldue as possible
in the crucible and repeat the hot 6 N HNO4-0.25 M A1(NOg),
treatment. Allow to cool and then fllter. Proceed to the ex-
traction procedure.

Water. Place 1 1. of the sample in 2 1.5 1. beaker and if
basle, neutralize with nitric acid. Add 15 ml of 70% HNO and
evaporate to 30-40 ml. Decant the solution through a filter,
such as Whatman no. 40, into a 100 ml beaker. Wash the 1.5 1.
beaker, the residue and the filter with 4 XN HNO. Evaporate the
combined solution in the 100 ml beaker to 5 ml. Add 20 ml of 4 N
HNO4, cover with a watch glass, and heat for 5 min. Transfer the
sample to a 125 ml cylindrical separatory funnel graduated at 30
ml. Wash the beaker with 4 N HNOg and transfer to the separatory
funnel, belng careful that the total volume in the separatory

funnel does not exceed 29 ml. Proceed to the extractlon procedure.

Extraction

Add 1.ml of 2 M KNO, to the sample in the 125 ml cylindrical
separatory funnel. Dilute to the 30 ml mark with 4 N HNO and
stir the solution briefly. Add 30 ml of 50# TBP in n-tetradecane.
Agltate the solution vigorously for 4 min with an air-driven
stirrer. Discard the acid portion (lower layer). Wash the TBP
portion with 4 N HNO, and agaln discard the acid portion. Back
extract with seven 15 ml portions of distilled water, collecting
the strip solution in a 150 ml beaker. Evaporate the combined
aqueous portions to 10-15 ml, then quantitatively transfer the
solution to a flamed stainless steel planchet. Allow to dry under
a heat lamp, flame the planchet to burn off organle residue, and
count on an a-gounter. Retaln for pulse-helght analysis if the

a-count exceeds a specified level.

PROCEDURE 9: Separation of Uranlum by Solvent Extraction with

Tri-n-octylphosphine Oxide.
Source: C. A. Horton and J. C. White, Anal. Chem. 30, 1779 (1958).

Abstract

A simple, rapld method for the determination of uranium in
impure aqueous solutions was developed. Uranium(VI) 1s extracted
by 0.1M trl-n-octylphosphine oxlde ln cyclohexane from a nitric
acid solution. A yellow color ls formed in an aliquot of the or-
ganlc extract by additlon of dlbenzoylmethane and pyridine in ethyl
alcohol. Interference by catlons 1s minimized or eliminated by
selective reduction, by fluoride complexatlon, or by absorbance
measurement at 416 mp rather than 405 mu, the wave length of
maxlmum absorbance, Interference by excess fluorlde or phosphate
1s eliminated by addition of aluminum nitrate before extraction.
The range of the method 1s 20 to 3000 ¥ of uranium ln the origlnal
solution, and the standard deviation is 2%.

Apparatus and Reagents

photometer, using 1.00-cm. Corex or slllica cells.

STANDARD URANIUM SOLUTIONS. A stock solutlon of 24.0 mg. of

PROCEDURE 10: Radiochemlcal Determlnation of Uranium-237.
Source: F. L. Moore and S. A. Reynolds, Anal. Chem. 31, 1080 (1959).

Abstract
A radiochemical method for the determination of uranium-237
is based on complexing the uranyl lon in alkaline solution with
hydroxylamine hydrochloride, followed by scavenglng wlth zilrconlum
hydroxlde and extraction of the uranlum from hydrochlorle acld
solution with trlisooctylamine-xylene. The technique has been
applied successfully to the determination of uranlum-237 1n

homogeneous reactor fuel solutions.

Preparation and Standardization of Uranlum Carrier
Welgh out approximately 50 grams of uranyl nitrate hexahydrate.

Dissolve and make to 1 liter with 2 M nltrlec acid. Standardize

the carrier by plpetting S5-ml. allquots into 50-ml. glase centrl-
fuge cones and preclpltating ammonium dluranate by addlng concen=-
trated ammonium hydroxide. Filter quantitatively through No. 42
Whatman filter paper and lgnite in porcelain cruclbles at 800°C.

for 30 minutes. Welgh as U30g.

294
PROCEDURE 10 . (Continued)

Procedure

In a 40-ml. tapered centrifuge tube add 1 ml. of uranium
carrier and 0.2 ml. of zirconium carrier (approximately 10 mg. per
ml. of zirconlum) to a sultable aliquot of the sample solution.
Dllute to approximately 10 ml,., mix well, and preclpltate ammonium
diurenate by the additlon of concentrated ammonium hydroxide.
Centrifuge for 2 minutes and dlscard the supernatant solution.
Wash the precipitate once with 15 ml. of ammonium hydroxide (1 to 1).

Dissolve the preclpltate in 1 to 2 ml. of concentrated hydro-
chloric acld solution, dilute to about 10 ml., add 1 ml. of
hydroxylamine hydrochloride (5 M), and mix well. Precipltate
zlrconlum hydroxlde by the addltlon of concentrated ammonium
hydroxide. Centrifuge for 2 minutes, add 0.2 ml. of zirconium
carrier, and stlr the supernatant solution, belng careful not to
disturb the precipitate. Centrifuge for 2 minutes. Add 0.2 ml.
of zlrconlum carrler and repsat.

Transfer the supernatant solution to another 40-ml. centri-
fuge tube, add several drops of phenolphthalein, and adjust the
pH to approximately 8 by adding concentrated hydrochloric acld
solution dropwise. Add an equal volume of concentrated hydro-
chloric acid solution and extract for approximately 0.5 mlnute
witha one-half volume portion of 5% (w./v.) triiscoctylamine-
xylene. Discard the aqueous phase. Wash the organle phase by
mixing for 0.5 minute with an equal volume portion of 5 M hydro-
chloric acld solution. Repeat the wash step. Strlp the uranium
from the organic phase by mlxlng thoroughly with an equal volume
portion of 0.1 M hydrochloris acld solution for 0.5 minute. Dlscard
the organlc phase.

Add 0.2 ml. of zirconium carrler, mix well, and repeat the
"above procedure, beginning with the precipitation of ammonium

dluranate.

295
PROCEDURE 10 (Continued)

Finally, precipltate ammonium diuranate by the additlon. of
concentrated ammonium hydroxide. Centrifuge for 2 minutes. De-
cant and discard the supernatant solution. Filter on No. 42 What-
man filter paper and ignite at 800°C. for 30 minutes.

Weigh the uranium oxide on a tared eluminum foll (0.0009
inch), fold, and place in a 10 x 75 mm. culture tube. Insert a
gultable cork and count the uranium-237 gamma radloactivity in a
well-type scintillation counter. Count the same day of the last
chemical separation.

Apply a blank correctlon if very low uranium-237 levels are
being determined. Determine this correction by taking the same
aliquot of uranium carrier through the exact procedure described
above. The blank correction 1s due primarily to the gamma radlo-

actlvlity assoclated wlth the uranium-235 in the uranlum carrier.

PROCEDURE 11: Separation of Uranlum and Blsmuth.

Source: A. Krishen and H. Frelser, Anal. Chem. 29, 288 (1957).
Editor's note: Uranium has been separated from a 5000~-fold
excess of bismuth by the following method. Uranlum is; however,
not completely extracted (only 98.48% at pH values greater than
6.5). If thls correction is applied, uranium 1s quantitatively

Severed by polarographic means within an experimental error
of *1%.

"Reagents
Acetylacetone. Commerclal acetylacetone was purified by
the method described by Stelnbach and Freiger.2

Procedure
Analysis. The method of Souchay and Faucherre,2 using 0.1M
EDTA and 2M sodium acetate as a supporting electrolyte, was found
to be suitable In the presence of dissolved acetylacetone. The
half-wave potentlal was shifted to -0.47 volt but the wave height .

was not affected.

296
PROCEDURE 11 (Continued)

Separation. Solutlons of uranyl sulfate containing 0.1 and
1.0 mg. of uranium were mixed with different amounts of bismuth
trichloride solution. A solution of the dlsodium salt of EDTA was
added to give a bismuth to EDTA ratio of 1 to 30. The pH of the
mixture was ralsed to 7.5 by careful addition of 1N sodium hydroxide.
Then approximately 10 ml. of acetylacetone was added and the mix-
ture shaken for 10 minutes. The acetylacetone phase was separated,
filtered, and made up to a volume of 10 ml., of which 2 ml. was
wlthdrawn by a plpet into a 10-ml. borosllicate glass volumetric
flask. The flask was very gently warmed until the liquid was re-
duced in volume to about 0.5 ml. Then the supporting electrolyte
was added and the resulting solution deaerated for 5 minutes in
a 10-ml. Lingane-Laltlnen H-type polarographic electrolysis cell.
The polarogram was then recorded and the concentration of uranium

found from sultable callbratlon curves.

PROCEDURE 12: Isolation and Measurement of Uranlum at the
Microgram Level.
Source: C. Le. Rulfs, A. K. De, and P. J. Elving, Anal. Chem.
28, 1139 (1956).
Abstract

A double cupferron separation of uranium using extraction
has been adapted to the micro level. Uranium(VI) does not extract
in the first stage, which removes many potentially interfering
elements. Uranium(IV), obtalned in the residual aqueous solution
by reduction at a mercury cathode, 1s simultaneously extracted as

the cupferrate into ether, from which it can be re-extracted into

297
PROCEDURE 12 (Continued)

nitric acid. A relatively simple one-plece glass apparatus is
used for all operations. The uranium recovery at the milligram
level in an initial 30-ml. sample was determined colorimetrically
as 94%. With 0.03 t0 0.13 ¥ of radioactive uranium-233 tracer

and 20 y¥ of natural uranium as carrier, the recovery is B6%;

the latter includes the additional step of electrodepositlon of
the uranium onto a platinum planchet prior to measurement by alpha
counting, which 1s only 94% complete, The decontamination possible
with this procedure was checked with 0.07 y quantitles of uranium-
233 in the presence of high mixed flsslon product activities; 85%
recovery. was obtained, contelning only 0.9% of the fission product
glpha activity (assumed to be uranium).

Apparatus
The reactlon cell and simple electrical c¢ircult used 1s

shown in the accompanying figure.

The electrolysls vessel, CG, 18 protected from meroury ions
diffusing from the working reference oalomel electrode, A, by a
medium glass frit between B and C, and a fine frit backed with
en agar plug between B and A. Between runs, cell C 1s kept filled
with saturated potassium ohloride solution.

The apparatus for the electrodepositlon of uranium onto
platinum disks or planchets and for alpha-counting measurement
of the resulting uranium plates have been described. Beta
aotivity was measured by a chlorlne-quenched argon-filled Gelger-
Muller counter (1.4 mg. per sq. om. of window) with a Model 165
scaler; a sointillation well counter with a thalllum-dctivated
godlum iodide crystal and a Model 162 scaler was used for gamma-
activity measurement of solutions (ca. 5 ml.) contained in a 13
x 150 mm. test tube. The scalers end counters are made by the
Nuclear Instrument and Chemlocal Corp. For examlnatlon of the

gamma-ray spectrum, a gamma-ray scintillation spectrometer (built

298
PROCEDURE 12 (Continued)

in the Department of Chemistry, Unlversity of Michigan) was used
through the courtesy of W. Wayne Melnke.

Reagents
All chemicals used were of C.P. or reagent grade unless

otherwise speclfied. The ethereal cupferron solution used (200
to 300 mg. of cupferron per 50 ml.) was actually a hydrogen oup-
ferrate solution; the ether and cupferron were mixed ln a mixing
eylinder with 5 to 10 ml. of 10 to 20% sulfuric acid and shaken

until dissolution was complete.

Procedures

Reductive Extraction. At the commencement of a run, brldge
B 1s flushed through stopcock 2 by filling B wlth fresh potasslum
chloride solution from the funnel through 1. C is drained and
rinsed; 1 1s left open for a time to flush the frit. With 3 closed,
4 to 5 ml. of triple-distilled mercury 1s placed in C. About 30 ml.
of uranyl sulfate solution (0.5 to 5 mg. of uranium and 0.5 to 1.5%
in sulfuric acld) 1s added and a potential of -0.35 volt vs.
S.C.E. 18 applied to the mercury. About 15 to 20 ml. of the
ether cupferron solution 18 added. Stirring 1s adjusted at Just
over the minimal rate for efficlent current flow (usually about
0.2 ma. flows without stirring and 1.2 to 2.6 ma. with stirring).

Stopcock 1 is opened for about 30 seconds at approximately
S5-minute intervals throughout the run to minlmlze any loss of
uranium into the bridge. At 15~ or 20-minute intervals, stirring
18 interrupted, the ether extract 1s bled through stopcock 4 into
cell D, and 15 to 20 ml. of fresh ether-cupferron solution 1s added.
Runs of 40- to 55-minute total duration appear to be adequate.
Three increments of ether-cupferron solution were usually used,
" followed By a 5=- to 10-ml. pure ether rlnse at the conclusion of
“the run. (See Note 1.)

slowly on stainless-steel counting trays that have had 1 drop of
anti-creeping solution evaporated at their centers.® Heat the
trays to redness in the flame of a Meker burner, cool and count.

PROCEDURE 15: Use of Ion Exchange Resins for the Determination
of Uranium in Ores and Solutions.

Source. 8. Fisher and R. Kunin, Anal. Chem. 29, 400 (1957).

Abstract

The separation of uranlum from the lons Interferlng with ite
analysls 1s accomplished by the adsorption of the uranium(VI) sul-
fate complex on a quaternary ammonium anion exchange resin. Inter-
ference of such lons as iron(III) and vanadium(V) is avoided by
thelr preferentlal reduction with sulfurous acid so that they, as
well as other cations, are not retained by the resin. Uranium is
eluted for analysls by dllute perchloric acid. The method is

applicable to both solutlons and ores.

Ore Solution

Two methods for the opening of uranlum-bearing ores were
Investigated 1n conjunction with the lon exchange separation. The
flrst 1s the standard digestion wlth hydrofluoric and nitric acids,
with subsequent evaporation to dryness followed by a sodlum car-
bonate fusion.2 The carbonate melt 1s dissolved in 5% sulfuric
acld to form a solution for the separation. A second method for
routine enalysls, designed to eliminate the need for hood facili-
tles and platinum veseels, involves an oxldatlive leach with an
acidic manganese(IV) oxide system. This procedure 1s given in
detail below. Other workers?, using the authors! separation
procedure, have recommended solution of the ore by treatment with

12M hydrochloric acid plus 16M nitric acid followed by fuming

307
PROCEDURE 15 (Continued)

with sulfuric acid to produce a suitable uranium solution for the
column influent.

Procedure. Welgh out samples of ore estimated to contain
an amount of uranium oxlde less than 100 mg. but sufficient to be
detected by the chosen method of analysis. Add 20 ml. of 20% by
volume sulfuric acld and 2 grams of manganese(IV) oxide. Heat
the mixture to bolling. Allow to cool to room temperature. Dilute
with approximately 50 ml. of water. Adjust to a pH between 1.0
and 1.5 by the dropwise addition of 20% sodium hydroxide. Filter
through fine-pore filter paper using two 10-m1. portions of water

to wash the residue on the paper.

Ion Exchange Separation

Apparatus. Tubes 0.5 inch in dlameter with high-porosity
sintered glass fllter disks fused to the lower end are used to
contain the resin, The rate of flow of solutions through the
tube 18 regulated by a screw clamp on rubber tubing below the
filter. Small separatory funhels are attached to the top of the
column to feed the sample and reagents.

Procedure. Convert a portion of quaternary ammonium anion
exchange resin (Amberlite XE-117, Type 2) of mesh size 40 to 60
(U.S. screens) to the sulfate form by treating a column of it with
10% sulfurlo acld, using 3 volumes per volume of resin. Rinse the
acld-treated resin with delonlzed water until the effluent 1s
neutral to methyl red. Drain the resin so prepared free of excess
water and store in a bottle. A 5-ml. portion of this resin 1s used
for a single analysis. The resin 18s loaded into the filter tube and
the bed so formed 1s backwashed with enough water to free it of
alr. After the resin has settled the excess water is drained off
to within 1 cm. of the top of the bed prior to the passage of the
sample through the bed.

Add 5 drops of 0.1% methylene blue to the partially neu-

308
PROCEDURE 15 (Continued)

tralized (pH 1.0 to 1.5) solution from the dissolved sodium ocar-
bonate melt or from the filtered manganese(IV) oxide leach. Add
6% sulfurous acid dropwise until the methylene blue is decolorized
and then add a 5-ml. excess. Pass the reduced pample through the
reain bed at a rate not exceeding 2 ml. per minute. Wash the sam-
ple contalner with two 10-ml. portions of water, passing the
washing through the resih bed at the same flow rate. Elute the
uranium with 50 ml. of 1M perchloric acid. Determine the uranium
content of the perchlorlec acid fraction colorimetrilcally by the
standard sodium hydroxide-hydrogen peroxide method® oi volumetri-
callyS. For colorimetric analysis standard uranium solutions
containing perchloric acld should be used in establishing the

curve.

Source: W. Ryan and A. F. Williams, Analyst 77, 293 (1952).
Abstract

A technique in inorganic chromatography, with alumina and
cellulose adsorbents ln the same extraotion column, 1s described
for the separation of uranium from minerals and ores. The pur-

pose of the alumina 1s to retain arsenic and molybdenum, which

as the extraction solvent.

METHOD FOR SAMPLES CONTAINING MOLYBDENUM OR ARSENIC OR BOTH
Solvent--Add 5 ml of concentrated nitric acid, sp.grs 1.42, to
each 95 ml of ether.

PREPARATION OF ALUMINA-CELLULOSE COLUMN--

The adsorptlon tube for the preparation of the column 1s a
glass tube about 25 em long and 1.8 cm in diameter. The upper
end 1s flared to a dlameter of about 8 ecm to form a funnel that
permits easy transfer of the sample. The lower end terminates
in a short length of narrow tubing and ls closed by a short
length of polyvinyl chloride tubing carrylng a screw clip. The
inside surface of the glass tube 1s coated wlth a sllicone in
the manner described by Burstall and Wells.2

Welgh 5 or 6 g of cellulose pulp into a stoppered flask and
cover 1t with ether-nltric acld solvent. Pour the suspension ln-
to the glass tube, agltate gently and then gently press down the
cellulose to form a homogeneous column. Wash the column wlth
about 100 ml of ether-nltric acld solvent and finally allow the
level of the solvent to fall to the top of the cellulose. Next
pour about 15 g of activated aluminium oxide’ on top of the
cellulose, pour on 30 ml of ether-nitric acld solvent and vig-
orously agltate the alumina with a glass plunger. Allow the
packing to settle. Allow the level of the ether to fall to the

surface of the alumina and the column 1s ready for use.

PROCEDURE 18: Determination of Microgram and Submicrogram
Quantities of Uranium by Neutron Actlvation Analysis.

Source: H. A. Mahlman and G. W. Ledlcotte, Anal. Chem. 27, 823
(1955).

Abstract

Miocrogram and submlcrogram quantities of uranium have been
determined in synthetic samples, ores, and solls by neutron
radloactivation analysis. The principles of the aotlvation
enalysip method used in this determination and the prooessing of
irradlated samples are dlscussed. This method of analysis 18 a
sensitive and specific method for determining uranium ln concen-
trations as mall as 0.1 q¢ per gram with a probable rélative
standard error of 10%. Concentrations of uranium in quantities
as small as 0.0001 ¥ per gram can be determined by neutron activ
atlqr analysis.

Radloactlivation Analysis of Samples that Contaln

Uranium

Nuclear Irradiation of Sample. Welghed portions of the
samples and the comparatlve standard are put into small quartz
tubes. The tubes are closed with cork stoppers that are wrapped
in aluminum. They are then irradiated in the reactor. After
irradiation, the samples are allowed to decay about 4 hours and
are then chemically processed as described below. The synthetic
samples used in thls laboratory had been processed by a fllter
paper partition chromatography technique. After the separation,
the paper was convenlently irradiated in short pleces of quartz
tubing whose openings were plugged by means of cork stoppers.

Chemical Separation of Neptunium-239. In most neutron
activation analyses, a chemical separation ls made to isolate
the radioactivity of the element from all other radloactlve
apecies in the sample. Usually an "isotoplc carrler"--a known

amount of the natural inactive element--13 added to the solutions

317
PROCEDURE 18 (Continued)

of both the lrradlated specimen and the comparison samples. The
solutions are then processed chemlcally to 1solate the carrier
and deslred radloelement from other elements and contaminant
radloactivitles. Small amounts of other elements are added as
holdback or eoavenging carriers to assist in the decontamination
process.

Although neptunlum-239 has a convenlent half life, lt does
‘not have a stable lsctope that can be used as an'isotoplc carrier.
However, Seaborg2 has shown that trace quantities of neptunium-
239 can be quantitatively carried on a nonisotoplc carrier, such
as cerlum. The method of analysis reported below uses lanthanum
as a nonlsotoplc carrier for the neptunium-239 radioactivity.

(See Note 1.)

Chemlcal Separation Procedure. PREPARATION. The irradiated
ore and soll speclmens are dissolved by digestion in a mixture of
concentrated nitrile, hydrofluoric, perchlorie, and sulfuric
acids. (Additional hydrofluoric acid can be added if a residue
of silica remains ln the bottom of the crucible.) After dissolu-
tlon, the sample 1s concentrated to heavy sulfuric acld fumes,
cooled, and transferred to a 15-ml. centrifuge tube. If a residue
(sulfate salts) remains after the transfer, the solution is cen-
trlfuged for 5 mlnutes, the supernatant transferred to another
tube, and the residue washed with 1 ml. of 1M nitric acid. The
wash 1s added to the supernatant and the residue discarded.
(Centrifugation is always for the stipulated time and at full
speed.) The sample 1s then further processed by the procedure
reported herein.

The irradiated synthetlc samples (paper chromatograms) are
processed by carefully igniting the paper contained in a porcelain
crucible in a muffle furnace. The residue 1s dissolved in about

0.5 ml. of concentrated nitric acid. After dissolution, the

318
PROCEDURE 18 (Continued)

sample 1s transferred to a 15-ml. centrifuge tube and the process-
Ing continued wlth the procedure reported herein.

PROCEDURE. Three (3.0) milligrams of lanthanum and 0.250
ml. of 5M hydroxylamine hydrochloride solution are added to the
supernatant solutlon and the mixture digested for 5 minutes wlth
occaslonal stirring. The solution 1s cautiously neutralized with
concentrated ammonium hydroxide to precipitate lanthanum hydroxide,
after whlch the mixture 18 centrifuged and the supernatant liquid
discarded.

The precipitate of lanthanum hydroxide is dissolved in 2 ml.
of 2M hydrochloric acld, and 1.0 mg. of strontium (added as a
solution of strontium nltrate to serve aes a holdback or scavenging
carrier) and 0.250 ml. of 5M hydroxylamine hydrochloride solution
are added to the solutlon. The solution ls agaln digested for
5 minutes with intermittent stirring, and 0.200 ml. of concentrated
hydrofluorle acld 1s added dropwlse to the solution to precipitate
lanthanum fluoride. After centrifugation, the supernatant liquid
1s discarded and the precipitate washed with 0.5 ml. of 1M hydro~
fluoric acild-1M nitric acid solution.

After washing, the lanthanum fluorilde precipltate 1s dissolved
in 0.5 ml. of saturated boric acld solution and 1.0 ml. of 6M
nitric acid. One (1.0) milliliter each of 10% potassium perman~
ganate solution and water are added to this solution, and the
resulting mixture ls agltated well and digested for 5 minutes.
Lanthanum fluoride 1s agaln precipitated with 0.250 ml. of con-
centrated hydrofluoric acld; the solution ls centrifuged and the
supernatant llquld transferred to another centrifuge tube. The
precipitate is washed with 0.5 ml. of 1M hydrofluoric acld-1M nitrile
acid solution and the wash combined with the supernatant liquid.
The preclpltate 1s discarded.

Three milligrams of lanthanum are added to the supernatant

319
PROCEDURE 18 (Continued)

liquid, and the solution 1s digested for 5 minutes and centrifuged.
An additional 3.0 mg. of lanthanum are added to the supernatant
liquid and the solution agitated and digested for 5 minutes wlthout
disturbing the first precipitate on the bottom of the tube; then
the solution is centrifuged and the supernatant liquid transferred
to another centrifuge tube. The precipitate 18 washed wlth 0.5
ml. of 1M hydrofluoric acld-1M nitrile aeld solution; centrifuged,
and the wash comblned wlth the supernatant liquid. The precipi-
tate 1s discarded.

One milligram of zirconium (added as a solution of zirconium
nltrate to serve as a holdback or scavenglng carrier) and 0.250 ml.
of 5M hydroxylamine hydrochloride are added to the solution and
the mixture agltated and digested 5 minutes. Three (3.0) milli-
grams of lanthanum and 2 ml. of 2M hydrofluoric acld are added
to the solution, and the solution is digested for 20 minutes and
then centrifuged. The supernatant liquid 1s dlscarded. The pre-
clpitate is washed with 0.5 ml. of 1M hydrofluoric acild-1M nitrie
acld solution, and the resulting mixture 1s centrifuged. The
wash solution 1s dlscarded after the centrifugation.

The precipitate 1s slurried in a small amount of 1M nitric
acid (about 0.5 ml.) and transferred to a small borosilicate glass
culture tube by means of a transfer pipet. The centrifuge cone
18 rinsed wlth three 0.5-ml. portions of IM nitric acld and the
rinses transferred to the culture tube. The tube 1s stoppered
wlth a cork stopper and the y radioactivity measured by a well-
type gamma scintillation counter.

The standard sample of uranium oxide (050g) is dissolved
in nitric acid and an aliquot of the solution processed under
the same condltlons as the specimen samples. The uranium content
of the sample 1n question 1s determined by equating the ratio of
the corrected neptunlum-239 radlioactlvity count in the unknown

and the corrected neptunium-239 radloactivity count in the standard
